Hunan Rice Embargo Lifted, Two Million Shi Shipped to Shanghai 133

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Sends Riverboats to Transport

Hunan has historically been a rice-producing region. In recent years, it has suffered from natural disasters and man-made calamities, resulting in barren fields. It had to purchase rice from outside to feed its people. This year, the rice harvest in various parts of Hunan was abundant. The Hunan province had banned the export of rice for many years. This year's autumn harvest was a bumper crop. The provincial government lifted the ban, allowing rice to be shipped out of the province. The first batch is about to arrive in Shanghai. The details are as follows, as investigated and recorded by our reporter.

Lifting of the Embargo. This year, Hunan province had a bumper harvest. The rice yield has increased several times compared to previous years. Based on investigation results, the Hunan provincial government determined that after meeting the food needs of the entire province, there was a large surplus. In order to adjust the grain shortage in neighboring provinces, it was decided to lift the rice embargo and allow export. The provincial government can also increase its revenue from rice export taxes. After discussion at the provincial affairs meeting, it was decided to initially allow two million shi to be exported. The decision to continue lifting the ban will depend on the situation in Hunan.

Dispatching Ships for Transport. The rice exported from Hunan will mainly be sold to Shanghai and Ningbo. All shipments will be delivered in Shanghai. Shanghai rice merchants have already gone to Hunan to purchase rice. Upon receiving the report, the Shanghai China Merchants Steam Navigation Company urgently sent personnel to Hunan to investigate. It was confirmed that the grain embargo had been lifted. The business department of the company then decided to dispatch large riverboat from the Yangtze River fleet to operate a direct Shanghai-Hunan route, specifically to transport the rice being exported. The first batch is expected to arrive in Shanghai at the end of this month.

Competition Among Ships. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has also borrowed iron barges from the Hanyang Arsenal and the Pingxiang Coal Mine to Changsha for transferring rice to ships. It also plans to add the Jiangjing boat to the Changsha route during periods of congestion to increase the tonnage of rice transported. Jardine Matheson, Butterfield & Swire, and San Peh Steam Navigation Company have all received the news and have dispatched riverboats to Changsha to compete to transport the two million shi of Hunan rice to Shanghai.

Cotton Weaving Industry Cancels All Subsidies 134

Realizing the Spirit of Labor-Management Cooperation

The cotton weaving industry in this city has been under the dual pressure of economic aggression from imperialism and domestic political turmoil for many years. It has been difficult to sustain itself even in normal times. Since last year's national flood, the purchasing power of the Chinese people has greatly decreased. The United Kingdom has also abolished the gold standard to increase exports, and the Japanese are also making every effort to dump goods. As a result, domestic goods factories with weak capital and high costs are facing stockpiles and are on the verge of collapse. To save themselves, they must reduce costs. The Silk and Cotton Weaving Industry Association sent a letter to the industrial unions of the cotton weaving industry in various districts, requesting that both labor and management coexist and prosper by reducing wages. After mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, the labor representatives understood the difficulties of the management and were willing to agree to cancel all

Subsidies and establish a three-article peace agreement. Yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau approved the original text of the agreement, which will be handed over to the Cotton Weaving Industry Association and the industrial unions. Amidst the surging waves of labor strikes, the cotton weaving industry workers are willing to cancel their existing conditions, which can be considered a model of labor-management cooperation. The original text of the agreement is recorded below: (1) The originally agreed upon labor-management conditions will remain in effect until the new conditions are revised. However, the factory is indeed experiencing poor business and is having difficulty sustaining itself. From the date of signing the agreement, the various subsidies stipulated in Articles 2 and 5 of the original conditions will be temporarily canceled. As for the yarn waiting subsidy in Article 6, the labor side expressed that it can be forgiven in fact. When the factory's business is truly restored to its original state, it will be submitted to the Bureau for approval and restoration. (2) The factory's request to reduce wages should not be discussed in view of the hardship of the workers. (3) The original methods of rewards and punishments will be cancelled for the time being. During the cancellation period, factory subsidies will still be allowed according to custom. Weaving workers will receive 30 cents of ocean money per month, and yarn shaking workers will receive 15 cents of ocean money per month for union dues. Attached are Articles 3, 5, and 6 of the original conditions. (4) The working hours are limited to ten hours and should not be wasted. If the factory needs to open night shifts, it is limited to three hours, and each person will be given 5 cents of ocean money for snacks in addition to wages. (5) In addition to handling meal money according to the old rules of each factory, weaving workers will receive an additional 50 cents of ocean money per month, and yarn shaking female workers will receive 30 cents of ocean money per month. (6) In case of waiting for warping and yarn doubling, the limit is three days. After three days, the factory will subsidize 25 cents of ocean money per day for work meals. If the workers do not go to the machine after three days, the work meal money will be deducted, but no further leave can be requested after three days, except in the case of natural disasters, illnesses, weddings, funerals, or special accidents.

The city government has decided that Councilor Luo Panhui will serve as the chairman of the arbitration committee. It has been decided to submit it to arbitration within a week.

Workers with Serious Illness Sent to Hospital. Since the 18th when the worker Hong Jiaben and others announced a hunger strike, because the capitalist side showed no awareness, Sun Handong and others continued the hunger strike. Although representatives from various parties forcibly fed them a little milk, they have not eaten a grain of rice until now, and their spirits have become extremely weak and reached a dangerous situation. Yesterday morning around 5:00 AM, the hunger-striking worker Lu Shiying moaned repeatedly, and her condition was particularly serious. The union hired a car to forcibly send her to the hospital for treatment.

Continuing to Set Off for Crying and Complaining. The Crying and Complaining delegation members Qi Weigen, Zhang Shiqi, and others, a total of 18 people, set off yesterday morning to the Chaozhou Shanghai Association, the China Women's National Salvation Federation, the Chinese Vocational Education Society, the Guangdong Provincial Association, the Sichuan Shanghai Association, the Citizens' Federation, the General Federation of Business Circles, the Hui Ning Shanghai Association, and other places to cry and complain about the pain of the workers. All sectors expressed sympathy and willingness to actively assist.

Meal Expenses Have Already Been Paid. The eighth installment of meal expenses for the workers, totaling 840 ocean dollars, should have been paid on Wednesday. The capitalist side made excuses to delay it for several days. Although the party and government agencies repeatedly negotiated, not only did they refuse to accept it, but they also made demands. Recently, in view of the tense atmosphere on all sides, the union representatives Xia Zhongzhao and Gong Zishen, together with Social Affairs Bureau representatives Wang Xianqing and Zhu Guilin, negotiated again at the Nanjing Road distribution office, and finally received the full amount.

Opinions of Central Government Representatives. The Central Party Department, in view of the labor-management dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Cooperative in Shanghai, which has been going on for a long time and has not been resolved, and that the workers have gone on hunger strike due to a lack of solutions, which is extremely pitiful, has sent Wu Zhongheng, the section chief of the Workers' Section of the Mass Movement Guidance Committee, and Zhang Jianbai to Shanghai, together with Shanghai-based investigator Jiang Hao, to the Sanyou Industrial Cooperative in Yinxianggang around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon to console the hunger-striking workers and persuade them to eat. They expressed to the hunger-striking workers that from the central government's perspective, whether from the standpoint of human feelings or the standpoint of the law, the central government believes that the capitalist side has no reason. Because the opening of a factory must be registered with the government, the closure of a factory should also be applied to the government for approval in advance. Whether to approve or not should be determined based on the situation. The expansion of the Hangzhou branch of the cooperative and the closure of the Shanghai general factory should not be possible. If these thousand workers lose their jobs, social panic will increase. Therefore, the central government ordered the Shanghai municipal government and the city party headquarters two weeks ago to force the capitalist side to resume work immediately. I, Wu, claim that after arriving in Shanghai, I immediately telegraphed the central government today, asking it to order the Shanghai party and government agencies to enforce the reply as soon as possible. The reply can arrive tomorrow. I am now in Shanghai and plan to immediately negotiate with the party and government agencies in this city to urge the capitalist side to come to its senses. I will also publish a statement of opinion to promote the capitalist side's awakening.

Cigarette Union Assistance. The Industrial Union of the Cigarette Industry in the Fourth District of this city convened an emergency representative meeting for the hunger strike of Sanyou workers. More than 100 representatives attended. Zhou Xuexiang was elected as the chairman. First, the chairman reported on the course of the Sanyou dispute and the hunger strike situation of the workers, and then discussed assistance methods: (1) Submit a petition to the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government, ordering the capitalist side of the Sanyou Industrial Cooperative to open the factory immediately to maintain the livelihood of the workers. (2) If necessary, the factories affiliated with our union will strike to assist. (3) Order affiliated members to provide as much assistance as possible. (4) The secret meeting ended.

Refuting the Capitalist's Statement. The Cotton Weaving Industry Union in the Seventh District issued the following statement in response to the absurd wording of the statement issued by Ji Jiannan, the director of the distribution office of Sanyou Cooperative, as reported in the Starry Night News: (1) After the January 28th Shanghai War, the Yinxianggang location was not designated as a combat zone. When the Japanese army entered the factory on February 17th, they divided the factory into two sections, moving the machinery and assets in the factory to the front section and hiring Russian police to guard it. The empty rooms in the rear section were where the Japanese army was stationed, and the capitalist side was subsidized 30 ocean dollars per day to cover the cost of water and electricity. Since the factory was outside the war zone, how could the machinery have been bombed? (2) The products produced by the general factory are of many types, such as 透凉罗纱 (Tou Liang Luo Sha, cool gauze), single-width bed sheets, towel quilts, free cloth, large and small bath towels, and various household items, not just tablecloths and curtains, which are not necessities. (3) The highest price for free cloth is 38 cents. (4) The capitalist side's annual inventory is always worth more than 3 million yuan, which is a habitual compensation and not overproduction. According to the accountant's investigation report in June of this year, the inventory value was 1.9 million yuan. The shameless Ji Jiannan lied and acted as a tiger, and his despicable personality is indescribable. Fearing that the public does not understand the facts, we have issued this statement to clarify the facts. Cotton Weaving Industry Union, Seventh District.

Various Sectors Express Condolences. Yesterday, those who went to express condolences to the hunger-striking workers included Fu Huaichen, Li Jingyi, and Chen Xiaomei, representing the soap and medicine industry union of the Ninth District, bringing 12 cans of milk, Ge Hecai, representing the publishing industry union, and representatives of the military uniform industry union, all bringing letters of condolence and persuading the hunger-striking workers to resume eating. However, the members of the hunger strike delegation resolutely refused to resume eating.

British Public Bus Workers' Strike Still Extremely Precarious 136

Workers Hold Two Meetings Yesterday

Hiring Lawyers to Assist Those Arrested

The strike of the British Public Bus workers has not seen any new developments as of yesterday, and the situation remains precarious. Two general meetings were held yesterday, and many important cases were resolved. The details are recorded below. Two general meetings. Yesterday morning at 8:00, all the striking workers held a general meeting at the Renhe Tea House on Wuding Road. More than 120 people attended. The suicide squad reported on the work situation and resolved to fight to the death. In the afternoon at 5:00, a general meeting was held again at the same location, and many important cases were resolved. Due to strict secrecy, the content could not be ascertained.

Assistance to Those Arrested. The day before yesterday, one worker, No. 34, was detained by the French police, and at the same time, the Public Concession police also detained one worker, No. 199. The arrested workers are still in custody and will be sent to court for trial tomorrow. The strike committee has hired a lawyer to appear in court to defend them.

Assaulting New Workers. Yesterday morning at 10:00, a No. 9 Public Bus drove to the intersection of Yangshupu Road and Pingliang Road, and was suddenly surrounded by many workers, who severely beat the new ticket-selling worker on the bus. The worker was seriously injured and sent to the hospital for treatment by an ambulance dispatched by the police. The workers who caused the incident have escaped and have not been caught.

Gunfire Last Night. Around 8:00 last night, when a No. 10 Public Bus arrived at the Xinqiao Station of the Sampan Factory on Maigen Road, a person wearing short clothes suddenly jumped out from the side of the road, holding a handgun in his hand, and aimed at the driver on the bus and fired a shot. Fortunately, the driver was unusually alert, heard the gunshot, and knew there was an accident, so he leaned back, causing his head to violently hit the glass window on the front of the bus, shattering the glass, and injuring his face and other parts. The person who fired the gun went west and disappeared in an instant. The injured driver's name is Bai Yukun, a 23-year-old from Yangzhou. He was sent to the Renji Hospital for treatment by Patrolman No. 2040 from the Xin Zha Police Station who arrived after hearing the news. Court Trial. At 8:20 PM on the 19th of this month, a British Public Bus Company No. 9, No. 108 Public Bus, traveling from east to west from the French Concession of Aiduya Road, arrived at the Dongxinqiao Station. Four striking workers were waiting there for the vehicle to arrive, and went forward to make trouble. When the four people saw the No. 108 bus driving to the station, No. 8 Zhang Bojian opened the door. While the passengers were getting on and off, one person got on the bus and punched Zhang in the face without asking why. Zhang was confused and did not understand what was happening. He was forcibly dragged down and beaten by three accomplices, causing his clothes to be torn and his body injured. At that time, the passengers and others did not understand what was happening and could not resolve the situation. A passenger in the car, Patrolman No. 539 of the Public Concession, caught sight of the situation, got out of the car, and intervened. Zhang managed to escape. The perpetrators fled in a panic. The Indian patrolman chased and shouted, and the suspects ran south towards Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession. Two Chinese patrolmen, No. 144 and No. 577, from the French Police Station arrived after hearing the noise and helped to arrest one person. The other three escaped. The arrested person was taken to the police station along with Zhang. The chief first ordered Patrolman No. 69 to send Zhang to Renji Hospital. After the doctor confirmed that the injury was minor, he applied medicine and left the hospital. Zhang returned to the police station, reported the assault, and requested an investigation. The chief questioned the defendant, who gave his name as Huo Zhongshan, a 26-year-old from Shandong, living in a shed on Wuding Road, Gorden Road. He was a ticket seller in the public bus company and denied the assault. He did not know the names of the three people who escaped, only knowing their numbers as No. 2, No. 34, and No. 278 ticket sellers. After the chief of the investigation section of the French Police Station, Xi, was able to determine that No. 2 was Tang Dongshan, living at No. 361 Yangzhou Road, No. 34 was Xuan Hengchang, living at No. 503 Tongji Road, Tiantong'an Road, and No. 278 was Li Rujiang, living at No. 1003 Hede Road. He immediately reported to the Second Special Court, signed an arrest warrant, and sent police officers and detectives to arrest them at their addresses. Tang had already escaped, and only Li Rujiang was caught. It was also found that Xuan Hengchang's original address had been moved during the war this spring, and his whereabouts were unknown. He escaped after the incident on the 19th. The next night (20th) at 8:00, he was arrested again in the Public Concession on Xin Zha Road for throwing stones at a public bus and was detained at the Xin Zha Police Station. He was immediately taken to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the Second Special District Court for investigation. In the afternoon at 3:00, Judge Wang Gangxu was promoted to the criminal court to conduct a preliminary hearing. First, Fei Xizhen, the lawyer of the police station, briefly stated the case, stating that the police station is now prosecuting according to Articles 158, 161, 197, 218, and 382 of the Criminal Law, disrupting order, endangering public security, damaging other people's property, and obstructing freedom, etc. However, the police station's procedures have not been completed, and a request is made to postpone the hearing for one week and allow the defendant to be temporarily detained. It was also stated that the police station received a report from the bus company today that the defendants had committed theft, but the police station has not yet investigated and prosecuted. Then, the plaintiff Zhang Bojian described the assault, but he could not remember the faces of the perpetrators because he was beaten and confused at the time. The official asked if he had any scars on his body, whether he had been treated, and whether he needed to be examined now. Zhang replied that he was treated at Renji Hospital at the time, and there was a medical certificate at the police station, but he is now fine and does not need to be examined. According to Indian Patrolman No. 539's testimony, he clearly saw the first defendant beating the plaintiff first, followed by the second and third defendants beating him together. When questioned, the defendant Huo Zhongshan stated, "At that time, I got off the No. 5 bus and walked south. I heard someone shouting 'robber' and was arrested. I did not commit the assault. I only sold tickets for a month in the public bus company. This time, six representatives initiated a request for the company to increase wages without getting a share of profit, which led to the strike." Li and Xuan also denied the assault. At this point, the official asked the witness, Indian Patrolman No. 539, "When they were beating him, did you see clearly whether the defendants were present?" The answer was, "I saw it clearly with my own eyes." The question was, "Can you guarantee it?" The answer was, "I can." He was then ordered to sign the guarantee. The court then announced that the hearing would be postponed and the defendants would be returned to custody.

Shuang Gong Silk Factory Labor Dispute Resolved 137

Wages Increased by One Cent Per Day

Factory Has Set a Date to Resume Work Tomorrow

Workers at the Fulunheng Shuang Gong Silk Factory at the end of Tianbin Road in Hongkou suddenly went on strike on the 19th. After several days of direct negotiations between labor and management representatives, a significant result was achieved yesterday. The factory has decided to resume operations tomorrow, and the union has also ordered workers to return to the factory at that time. The details are recorded below: Cause of the Strike. The Fulunheng Shuang Gong Silk Factory has a total of 216 silk reeling machines. Manager Shen Zupei, seeing that most of the Shuang Gong silk factories in the city have closed down and the price of Shuang Gong silk has slightly recovered, in order to meet market sales needs, specially modified 108 of the original single-eye silk reeling machines (i.e., each machine reels only one piece of silk) into double-eye machines (i.e., each machine reels two pieces of silk) in early July. The wages of the workers on the double-eye machines were increased to 45 cents, while the wages of the remaining 108 single-eye machine workers remained at 42 cents per day and were not increased. As a result, some workers expressed dissatisfaction and suddenly went on strike at 1:00 PM last Friday, and all the workers in the factory joined the strike.

Mediation Process. After the strike occurred, the workers immediately sent more than ten representatives to report to the Fourth District Silk Reeling Industry Union and requested negotiations with the capitalist to increase wages and improve treatment. The union sent directors Chen Xipou and Zhu Xizhang, and cadre Lu Xusheng, to negotiate with the capitalist representative Shen Zupei. After repeated negotiations and consultations, an agreement was reached at 4:00 PM yesterday (the 22nd). The result was that the wages of the single-eye machine workers were increased by one cent per day to 43 cents, and the wages of the double-eye machine workers remained at 45 cents. Any differences in the price of silver were calculated in ocean dollars. Working hours should be handled in accordance with the rules of the Dan Gong silk factory. The labor and management representatives expressed their agreement, and the strike was resolved.

Resuming Work Tomorrow. After the labor and management negotiations reached an agreement, the union found it difficult to notify all the workers who were scattered in various places in a timely manner. After consultation with the capitalist, it was decided to resume operations tomorrow (the 24th) morning. The union also notified all workers to return to work at that time. It is reported that the union has assigned personnel to be present at the factory when work resumes to maintain order.

Three Foreign Telegram Bureaus' Reply to Workers Yesterday 138

Rejecting Demands

The entire group of delivery workers at the Da Gong She, Yun Da Bei Da, and Eastern Pacific three telegram bureaus, due to demands for improved treatment and increased wages, sent a letter to the company manager on the 16th of this month, presenting six conditions, with a deadline for a reply yesterday. The company authorities, yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, officially replied in writing, rejecting all the conditions proposed by the workers. However, the workers do not seem to be going on strike immediately. Details are recorded as follows:

Company's Reply: After the Da Bei Da, Eastern Pacific three telegram bureaus received the letter from the delivery workers requesting improved treatment and increased wages, they gave a written reply yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM as follows: "To our respected colleagues, regarding your letter of the 19th of this month, written in block letters, in addition to what has already been explained verbally, we now specifically certify as follows: that our company's concern for the generous wages issue is as always, we are willing to begin an investigation. As for the results of the investigation, we will notify you within a reasonable period of time. At the same time, this company would like to solemnly state that the actions you are about to take are indeed dangerous and would like to solemnly warn you, that you are taking a significant risk, losing your current good job, generous wages, rice price subsidies, monthly bonuses, annual bonuses, sick leave wages, annual leave, and old-age subsidies, etc." This is addressed to all delivery workers of the Da Bei Telegraph Company, respectfully from Bolsen, by order of the General Manager. Also, the letter addressed to the Eastern workers was signed by Manager Bolade, and the content is the same as the letter above.

Workers' Statement: According to a statement issued by a responsible person from the workers' side to the Da Gong She reporter, "The company's so-called generous wages are only 29 yuan per month, and the lowest amount is only 18 yuan. As for the rice price subsidy, it only applies when the rice price reaches 14 yuan or more, and the company subsidizes one yuan. This amount is very small each day, at most one yuan per month, and as little as six or seven jiao of silver. The company has never issued bonuses. Workers' annual leave is only granted for one week per year after working for three full years; otherwise, it is not allowed. As for old-age subsidies, there are no regulations at all. The reply says, etc., are all fabricated facts, terms that obscure the outside world. The workers' vital interests are at stake, and in order to demand improved treatment, we are determined to take effective action to prompt the company authorities to realize this," etc.

National Coal Freight Rate Increase Postponed for Another Three Months 143

The National Mining Federation, considering that the cost of domestic coal is relatively high and cannot compete with Japanese coal, specially petitioned the Ministry of Railways to request a reduction in freight rates, but failed to obtain approval. The Ministry of Railways took advantage of the slack summer freight season to increase coal transport plan, but coal merchants were unable to realize this plan due to capital constraints. In order to encourage the production and sales of domestic coal, the Ministry of Railways specially extended the freight rate increase for another three months.

Reduction of Freight Rates Not Approved: The Ministry of Railways replied to the National Mining Federation's petition for a reduction in freight rates, saying that the main reason for the higher cost of coal mines operated by Chinese is the outdated production tools and poor technology, which has nothing to do with freight rates. The way to rescue them is to innovate production tools and technology; otherwise, simply reducing freight rates will be difficult to achieve. On the railway side, the current freight rates are not enough to make a profit. If they are reduced further, they will not be enough to maintain the road.

Increase in Coal Transport Not Successful: Since November of last year, the Ministry of Railways ordered all railway bureaus to temporarily suspend the price increase for three months, and subsequently extended the period repeatedly. Therefore, although it did not agree to reduce freight rates, it set another plan, ordering all railway bureaus to take advantage of the slack summer freight season to increase coal transport, and separately ordered all coal merchants to take advantage of this period of suspended freight rate increases to transport coal widely in order to avoid difficulties with vehicles in the winter. Now that the summer is about to end, coal merchants have encountered difficulties in terms of capital and time and have been unable to increase coal transport. The Coal Industry Guild has replied to the railway bureau by letter, stating the difficult situation, already reported in various newspapers, that the planned plan cannot be realized.

Freight Rate Increase Postponed: Since the plan to transport coal in the summer failed, and the suspension period is about to expire, the Ministry of Railways believes that it is necessary to postpone the increase again in order to rescue domestic coal merchants. It specially telegraphed all railway bureaus, ordering them to extend the period for another three months from this month. The railway bureau's document stated: "Since the East Province Incident occurred last year, various places have boycotted the import of Japanese coal, and the supply of domestic coal has fallen short of demand. In order to encourage the production and sales of domestic coal and relieve the coal shortage in the Yangtze River, the Ministry temporarily suspended the increase in coal transport rates on all roads for three months. It is estimated that the Jiaoji Railway implemented this on November 1st of last year, and the Jinghu, Huhangyong, Qingnanxun, Xiang'e, Pingsui, Longhai, Jinpu, Pinghan, and other eight roads implemented this on November 21st of last year. Since then, the periods have expired repeatedly, and the Ministry has repeatedly extended them and ordered compliance. Now, in order to relieve domestic coal and resist the dumping of Japanese coal, the Ministry will continue to extend the period for another three months from the 1st and 21st of this month (omitted below)."

International Trade Bureau Investigates National Industries 144

First Investigate Five Provinces, Estimated Completion in Two Years

Jiangsu Province's Investigation Has Been Completed in Several Counties After Implementation

In order to understand the situation of national industries and seek fundamental relief, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce specially launched a national industry survey, ordering the Shanghai International Trade Bureau to be responsible for the implementation. The bureau has recently complied with the order and is sending personnel to first investigate the five provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Hubei, and Hebei, and then go to other places for investigation. It is estimated that the investigation of the five provinces will be completed in two years. At that time, a special volume will be published. The industry in the entire Jiangsu province is under investigation. Director He Bingxian gave an important speech to the Xin Sheng News Agency yesterday regarding this matter, which is recorded as follows:

Investigation Area: The International Trade Bureau received the order from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce one month ago. At that time, Director He immediately proceeded actively and planned the detailed methods for this matter. It was decided to investigate the five provinces of Su, Zhejiang, Yue, E, and Ji within the national territory, and among the five provinces, to first engage in the investigation of Jiangsu province. Since the tenth of this month, investigators have been dispatched to various parts of Su province to proceed. Because of the public's full support, the investigation is progressing smoothly. As of yesterday, the places that have been investigated include Kunshan, Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, Jiangyin, Longtan, Nanjing, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Jintan, Changshu, Ze, Wujiang, Chuansha, Lili, and Lishui. It is estimated that the entire Jiangsu province can be investigated completely within three months, and the Chinese report will be published in November, and the English report will be published in December.

Investigation Personnel: The specialists for investigating national industries, Zhao Jian and Xiao Guozou, two staff members from the Statistics Section of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, worked together with the investigation specialists from the International Trade Bureau, Hou Houpei, Lu Guoxiang, Feng Hefa, Xie Ze, Yao Fangren, Jiang Xuekai, Ma Jibo, etc. They worked together, and Hou Houpei was recommended as the director. Currently, all of them have been dispatched to various places to engage in the investigation.

Investigation Types: The types of investigation are as follows: (1) Agricultural Economic Investigation, divided as follows: A. Total area of the county and soil rainfall, classification of farming households, etc., B. Agricultural workers, agricultural capital, agricultural tools, E. Cooperatives, (2) Investigation of Household Industries Attached to Farm Households: A. Main producing areas, B. Annual output, G. Raw materials used, D. Source of raw materials, E. Production season, F. Manufacturing aspects, G. Uses H. Application equipment, I. Price per unit, J. Trading habits K. Business organization, M. Main sales locations, N. Taxes, O. Improvements and others, (3) Industrial Investigation: A. Factory name, B. Organization, C. Capital, D. Number of employees, E. Source of workers, F. Work efficiency, G. Raw materials, H. Production situation, I. Sales market J. Equipment description, (4) Investigation of Financial Insurance and Warehousing Industries: A. Name, B. Establishment date, C. Category, D. Organizational nature, E. Capital, F. Public reserve fund, G. Main business, H. Annual turnover, (5) General Economic Situation Investigation: A. History of merchants, B. Currency in circulation, C. Annual import and export goods, (6) Investigation of Materials and Raw Materials: A. Animals and plants and their products, B. Reading materials (the above are general outlines). Director He Discusses: A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Director He Bingxian yesterday. According to the discussion, this investigation of national industries by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce is an unprecedented move in our country's construction cause. This is because our country has never conducted an investigation of national industries before. Twenty years ago, Japan published a book specifically about the industrial investigation of our country. However, it has been a long time since then, and it is different from the current situation. The purpose of this investigation, in general, is: (1) Internally, our country's industries are declining and urgently need to seek relief methods. However, in order to seek remedies, we must understand the industrial situation in various parts of the country, so that we know where the shortcomings are, so that we can determine the direction for improvement based on the situation of the national industrial economy. (2) Externally, to make the countries of the world understand the economic and commercial situation of China. At the same time, if there are countries that want to investigate the situation in China, they can also use this to answer. Because one of the most difficult points at present is that foreigners who observe China often ask about the industrial situation and have no way to answer. As for this investigation of the five provinces, it is estimated that it will be completed within two years. Afterwards, other provinces will be investigated.

Zheng Baozhao Discusses Railway Responsible Transportation 148

Coordinating with the Principle of People's Livelihood

Seeking Happiness for the Entire Society

The Ministry of Railways' implementation of responsible transportation this time is related to the national economy, and its significance is extremely important. The Jinpu, Jinghu, and Huhangyong roads have been set to implement this from September 1st. The reporter specially inquired about the personal opinions of Zheng Baozhao, director of the car affairs department of the two roads. Now he has given the following speech: "According to the general situation of railway responsible transportation, I have briefly discussed a few points in the last speech. Now I will further discuss the relationship between railway responsibility and merchants, manufacturing industries, and all aspects of society. First, the railway implements responsible transportation.

After the goods are delivered, the railway is fully responsible along the way. Merchants can save the trouble of various procedures and avoid unexpected losses. Merchants can use the bill of lading issued by the railway to mortgage it to the bank. Since the bank knows that the railway is responsible, it will be happy to accept it. The financial aspect can be extra circulated, and merchants can also rely on financial circulation to increase trade and adequately operate. Moreover, the goods are transported by the railway, which can eliminate the illegal commissions of intermediaries caused by the railway's irresponsibility in the past. The cost of goods transportation can be reduced compared to before. Second, regarding the manufacturing industry, due to the reduction in transportation costs, sales are becoming more and more widespread, and the amount of production can be increased at a high speed. According to economic principles, the wider the production, the lower the cost per unit of production (Perunttcosi). This is mutually causal, and industry and commerce can be developed extraordinarily. Third, in terms of society, the development of industry and commerce requires more and more workers. Workers can have work to do, which can solve part of the unemployment panic. Social order can become tranquil, and the number of production increases. The cost of production and transportation is reduced, and the market goods, according to the law of supply and demand, must fall in price. The people in society can obtain inexpensive goods, increase the purchasing power of money, and gradually reduce the level of living. This is in line with the Prime Minister's principle of people's livelihood. Therefore, responsible transportation is for the sake of happiness for the entire society and is not for the benefit of a few people. As for increasing the freight rate by 10%, it is only to compensate for the losses after responsibility and to add the need for employee equipment. It is completely different from the general increase in freight rates. Moreover, before the implementation of responsible transportation, the illegal commissions borne by the merchants often accounted for more than 20% to 30% of the freight. This time, we have cleared up the accumulated malpractices, and the increase is only 10%. It is obvious which one gets the better deal. At the beginning of this implementation, I urgently hope that all parties will give assistance so that there will be satisfactory results," and so on.

National Railway Freight Car Transportation Regulations (Continued) 149

Article 28: Changes in the Calculation of Freight Charges. In the event of a change as described in Article 24, freight charges shall be calculated according to the following items, and any difference or surplus in the freight charges already collected shall be collected or refunded separately: (1) Interrupted transportation: When requesting interrupted transportation, the freight for the section already transported shall be collected. (2) Change of destination station: For goods whose destination station is changed, if the goods must be transported forward or backward from the station where the goods are located, or if they must enter another line, the freight calculation method shall be as follows: first, add the mileage between the original departure station and the station where the goods are located to the mileage between the station where the goods are located and the newly designated destination station, and then calculate the freight according to the total mileage. (3) Return to the original station: When returning to the original station, the freight for the distance already traveled and the return trip shall be collected according to the schedule. Article 29: Changes in the calculation of miscellaneous freight charges. The following miscellaneous charges and expenses incurred due to changes shall be calculated separately: (1) Loading and unloading fees incurred due to changes. (2) When canceling consignment, the storage fee for the goods from the time the goods storage receipt is issued until the time the goods are taken out. However, if the first consignment is canceled and the goods are not moved out of the yard, and it is stated that the goods will still be consigned within 24 hours, the storage fee may be waived. However, for the second cancellation of consignment, regardless of whether the consignment is continued or not, the storage fee shall be calculated from the time the goods are moved into the freight yard until the time the goods are moved out or the consignment is continued. (3) When stopping loading, the detention fee for the vehicle from the time the vehicle is allocated until the time the railway receives the notice to stop loading (every hour or less than an hour shall be calculated according to the vehicle's load capacity, with one dime of ocean silver collected for each metric ton, including day and night). (4) In the event of interrupted transportation, the storage fee for the goods, the detention fee for the vehicle, and the switching fee (a total of two yuan of ocean silver shall be collected for the switching fee for each vehicle that is disconnected midway) from the time of stopping until the departure station receives other change notices. (5) All expenses incurred in the handling of Article 26. Article 30: Calculation of freight and miscellaneous charges for goods delayed in transit. In the event of a natural disaster or accident that causes a delay in railway transportation and cannot be restored within the shortest period, the railway shall immediately investigate and determine that goods that have been prepared for shipment and must pass through the disaster-stricken area shall not be loaded. If the goods have already been loaded and the fees have been collected, the consignor shall be notified to unload the goods, and the full freight shall be refunded, except for the miscellaneous fees that should be collected. Regardless of whether the goods have been loaded or not, if the consignor requests to transport the goods to a certain station that does not pass through the disaster-stricken area and there are still trains passing through, the railway may still transport the goods, but the difference between the freight already collected and the freight to the newly designated destination station shall be calculated and collected or refunded separately. In the event of the disaster described in the preceding paragraph, if the goods have been transported to a midway station and are detained, the railway shall immediately notify the consignor and inquire about the disposal method of the goods, and handle them separately according to the following methods: (1) If the consignor requests to continue transportation as soon as traffic is restored, it must be determined by the railway that the transportation is indeed likely to be restored in the shortest period. (2) If the consignor requests to return the goods to the original departure station, the railway shall return the goods free of charge and refund all the freight it has collected. (3) If the consignor requests to transport the goods to a certain station (not the original departure station), the railway shall calculate the difference between the freight from the original departure station to the originally designated destination station and the freight from the original departure station to the newly designated destination station, and collect or refund the difference separately. (4) If the consignor requests to unload the goods at the midway station, the railway shall refund the freight for the un-transported distance, and all miscellaneous fees required for stopping or changing transportation at the midway station shall not be collected. However, the request in item 4 shall be subject to approval by the railway, and the fees in items 1, 2, and 3 shall be calculated and collected in accordance with the regulations. Article 31: Inspection of Goods. When goods transported by the railway are delivered to the destination station, if the consignee believes that there is a suspicion of loss or damage to the goods, they may request the railway to inspect them and pay the inspection fee in accordance with the regulations. However, if the railway is responsible for the loss or damage of the goods, the inspection fee may be waived. If the railway discovers that the goods are lost, damaged, or have suspicious traces, it shall request the consignee or consignor to inspect them together, and the inspection fee shall be waived. However, the railway may also conduct inspections directly when necessary and notify the consignor or consignee of the inspection results. Article 32: Goods Unclaimed or Refused by the Consignee. If goods are transported to the destination station and no one claims them, or if the consignee refuses to accept them, the railway may temporarily store the goods in the freight yard and collect storage fees (if the goods are damaged due to railway negligence and the consignee refuses to accept them, the damaged goods may be exempted from storage fees, but the undamaged goods shall still be subject to storage fees), and handle them separately according to the following items: (1) If the goods have been transported to the destination station for more than ten days and no one has claimed them, or if the consignee refuses to accept the goods, the railway shall immediately notify the consignor and inquire about the disposal method of the goods. However, for items that are easily perishable or goods of particularly low value that the railway believes are insufficient to guarantee the freight and miscellaneous fees that should be paid, the railway may sell them at auction or dispose of them by other methods at any time. (3) If the consignee comes to claim the goods before the consignor's response to the above notice is received, the original goods shall be delivered, and the consignor shall be notified again (to be continued).

Public Burial of Tian Tong 150

Hubei Province Sends Steamer to Shanghai to Receive the Coffin

Mr. Tian Ziqin, a veteran of the Kuomintang and former member of the National Government, passed away at sea due to overwork in July two years ago. When the Central Government heard of this, it was extremely shocked. The Central Party Headquarters and the National Government, in recognition of Mr. Tian's contributions to the Party and the country, ordered Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun by telegram to lower the flag to mourn and to discuss preferential treatment. Commander-in-Chief Chiang, upon hearing the news at the front, ordered Shanghai Garrison Commander Xiong Shihui to assist in handling the funeral. Furthermore, the 118th Central Standing Committee passed a resolution for a public burial and instructed the Executive Yuan to order the Hubei Provincial Government to handle the matter. After receiving the order, the provincial government, together with Mr. Tian Huan, Mr. Tian Ziqin's brother, surveyed and designated Hongshan in Wuchang as the burial site. They also organized the Hubei Provincial Government Preparatory Committee for the Public Burial of Mr. Tian Ziqin, with members of the provincial government as ex officio members. The tomb construction project was designed by the Construction Department, and the project was quite extensive and the design magnificent. The mountain terrain was grand and the scenery beautiful, making it an unprecedented mausoleum in Hubei Province. The public burial was originally scheduled for November last year, but it was postponed to this spring due to the flood. It was then postponed again due to the Japanese invasion of Shanghai. Recently, President of the Judicial Yuan Ju Zheng formally telegraphed the Hubei authorities, inviting Tian Huanmin back to Hubei to discuss the matter with Director He Chengjun, Chairman Xia Douyin, Chairman of the Public Burial Committee Zhu Huaibing, and Vice Chairman Kong Geng. It has now been decided that the public burial will take place at Shen Shi (3-5 PM) on September 20. The Hubei government will send a special steamer to Shanghai to receive the coffin. It is expected that the steamer will depart around the 10th of next month. As Mr. Tian was a veteran of the Kuomintang, there will definitely be grand and solemn activities at that time.

Results of the Two-Day Minhang Yacht Race 155

The Minhang Yacht Club held its scheduled race on Saturday and Sunday. There was only one race on Saturday and two races on Sunday. The race situation is recorded below. In the race on Saturday, only three yachts participated: (He Dafu) driving yacht No. 3, (Hua Tuosheng) No. 4, and (Xiang Liansheng) No. 6. At 3:40 PM, the flag was raised at the starting line (Puhua Garden) and the yachts set off. No. 3 crossed the starting line first, followed closely by No. 6, and No. 4 was the last to set off. No. 3 passed the first marker on the Pudong bank downstream, turned to the second marker on the opposite bank, and then returned upstream, crossed the starting line, and reached the third marker, and then turned back to the starting line to finish. Nos. 6 and 4 never caught up. Therefore, the gold medal (a silver cup) was awarded to He Dafu. The first race on Sunday started at 12 noon. Six yachts participated: (Hai Si) driving No. 3, (Hua Tuosheng) No. 4, (Xiang Shouze) No. 6, (Wang Yanqing) No. 9, (Gu Chongqing) No. 10, and (A Tuojin Si) No. 11. At the sound of the order, No. 6 crossed the starting line first, followed closely by No. 3, then No. 10 and No. 9. Unexpectedly, No. 9 collided with No. 10, resulting in disqualification. At this time, No. 3 overtook No. 6, with Nos. 10, 4, and 11 behind. No. 6 was disqualified for touching the first marker. However, the wind was extremely light at this time, and yachts Nos. 10, 4, 11, and 3 could not reach the second marker, resulting in their disqualification midway. Only yacht No. 3 was driven properly and reached the finish line. The second race on Sunday started at 3:30 PM. The participants were (Hai Si) driving No. 3, (Hua Tuosheng) No. 4, (Xiang Shouze) No. 6, A Tuojin Si) No. 9, (Gu Caiwen) No. 10, and (Gu Chongqing) No. 11. In the sound of the police whistle, Nos. 6 and 11 drove side by side in the lead. Soon, No. 11 overtook No. 6 and reached the first marker, followed by Nos. 6, 9, and 10, while Nos. 4 and 3 fell behind. After passing the third marker, No. 10 rushed out, and Nos. 9, 6, and 11 went side by side. However, at the finish line, the bow of No. 10 exceeded No. 11 by about a foot in an instant. The results were most exciting at this time. Amidst the applause of the audience, the gold medal was awarded to Mr. Gu Caiwen.

Local News Two

Yun Huifang Case Not Heard Yesterday 157

Police Lodge an Appeal Against Bail

High Court Summoned the Entire Case File

Therefore, the Trial Could Not Proceed Yesterday

Lawyer Zhao Chen Speaks on the Appeal

Yun Huifang was prosecuted by the Public Concession Bureau of Public Works to the First Special District Local Court for using letter bombs to warn unscrupulous merchants who sold enemy goods, and was granted bail after a guarantee was provided by the business. Yesterday morning was the third scheduled hearing of the case. The Police Department of the Bureau of Public Works, in order to maintain order and tranquility in the court, still dispatched a large team of armed Chinese, Western, and Indian police, thirty to forty in number, led by Western Inspector Fan Pengnian, driving a large red police car with a machine gun installed on the front of the car. At 8 AM, they drove to the front of the First Special Court and stopped on the east side of North Zhejiang Road on Qipu Road, with the front of the car facing the court. Inspector Fan then ordered half of the armed police to be deployed on the left and right sides of the car, and the rest were sent to the court to assist the bailiffs in dispersing the posts. The first courtroom on the third floor, where the case was being heard, was also assigned additional bailiffs to patrol, and several senior Western police officers guarded the doors outside the courtroom. Anyone who was not involved in the case was not allowed to enter. The security was unprecedented. After 8 AM, Yun Huifang and her lawyer arrived at the court one after another. Only a very small number of representatives from various groups and members of the public were allowed to enter the courtroom. Those who arrived after 8:30 AM were all blocked outside the courtroom, giving them a sense of being so close yet so far away. Fortunately, they all knew to maintain order, so although three to five hundred people gathered in the narrow alley in front of the door and by the escalator for a time, there was no shouting or abrupt behavior. At 9:30 AM, Presiding Judge Feng Shide, Chief Prosecutor Wang Zuze, and Female Clerk Tang Weishu took their seats. Chinese Detective Zhao Bingkun, who was handling the case, brought the defendant Yun Huifang to the defendant's box. Yun had a smile on her face and was composed. First, Ru Baoyi, the prosecutor's lawyer for the police, stood up and stated that the police had filed an appeal with the Second High Court against the previous court's decision to grant bail to the defendant. The appeal case has not yet been resolved by the Second High Court, so the case cannot proceed today and should be postponed until the appeal issue is resolved. Defendant's lawyer Zhao Chen immediately expressed agreement to the postponement. Judge Feng then declared that the case file had been summoned by the High Court and had not yet been returned, so it must be postponed. As soon as the High Court decides to return the case file, the court will be opened. He then wrote a note stating that the case file had been summoned by the High Court and would be scheduled for trial after it was returned. Yun Huifang then left the defendant's box and left the court with representatives from various groups. The audience then dispersed, and all security measures were also withdrawn, returning to normal. It was only ten o'clock at this time. Lawyer Zhao Chen made a statement regarding the appeal against Yun's bail, stating (above omitted): "Article 67 of the Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that the power to detain the defendant during the trial belongs to the presiding judge or the assigned judge. Article 74 stipulates that the defendant may at any time apply for the termination of detention upon providing bail. Although Article 414 allows the parties to appeal to the direct superior court if they are dissatisfied with the court's ruling, the legislative intent of Article 415 is to ensure the defendant's status. The current spirit of the Criminal Procedure Law places great emphasis on the defendant's interests. The police's position, in terms of assisting the judiciary, is similar to the public security bureau in the mainland, and in terms of representing the prosecution, it is similar to the prosecutor of the court. We have never heard of a public security bureau transferring a suspect to the court and then appealing because the court granted bail, nor have we heard of a prosecutor filing a public prosecution and then disagreeing because the trial judge granted the defendant bail and appealing to the superior court. This strange phenomenon is not seen in the mainland, but it has become a bad example in the concession, which is not a way to protect the defendant's interests. In fact, according to the agreement of the Chinese courts in the Public Concession, the police only have a portion of the power of investigation and public prosecution. The prosecutor can still appear in court to state his opinion and cannot go beyond the scope of the agreement and the Criminal Procedure Law, and have all the powers that the prosecutor has or does not have. It is hoped that the police authorities will respect the interests of the defendant and accept well-intentioned advice to remedy the future. Otherwise, it may be suspected of interfering with the trial. Moreover, Yun has provided bail twice and has never escaped or failed to appear, and there is no risk of collusion or destruction of evidence, and the suspicion of her crime is not as serious as the police claimed. There is no question that bail should be granted. The police lawyer is honest and upright, why should he oppose it and why should he appeal, just to delay the progress of the case? As for the substantive issue of the Yun case, I have long determined it to be a continuous crime during the first hearing, but I did not want to express my opinion casually because the debate period had not arrived."

Pole Attempts to Rape Chinese Woman 160

Evidence Conclusive

Crime Cannot Be Pursued

The Pole, Du Boliewa Sigen (transliteration), is employed at a leather and soap factory established by a Westerner in Caojiadu. At about 9 AM on the 20th of this month, a neighbor, Strong Wu, a native of Suzhou, went out to wash clothes and passed by the entrance of the leather and soap factory. Unexpectedly, she was forcibly dragged in by the Pole under the eyes of nearby residents, causing a great uproar. The incident was reported to the nearby police, who entered the factory to investigate and saw the Pole, Du Boliewa Sigen, hugging Strong Wu on his lap, and Strong Wu shouting for help, claiming rape. The police obtained the Pole, who indeed intended to rape the Chinese woman, and took the Pole, Du Boliewa Sigen, and Strong Wu to the Sixth District Headquarters for investigation. After questioning, Director Zhang learned that the Pole did intend to rape the woman. Because he was a citizen of a country without a treaty, he was sentenced to be handed over to the Public Security Bureau for legal proceedings.

Dajilun Tugboat Causes Accident 161

Girl Falls into the River and Drowns

The Dajilun tugboat, which towed a barge loaded with iron to Wuxi the day before yesterday, unexpectedly sailed to the Yejidun area in western Shanghai. The tugboat wanted to turn, but the helmsman lacked experience, causing the ship to list. The small barge being towed bore the brunt of the accident, causing all six people on the barge, including the family of Yue Haiqing, to fall into the water, and the boat capsized. Rescue efforts were made, but Yue's 11-year-old niece, Yue Xiujin, drowned. The body was not recovered until the afternoon and was taken to the Local Court yesterday for examination. Prosecutor Xie and others examined the body according to the law and confirmed that the body was indeed drowned. It was ordered that the body be taken for burial and await investigation.

Military Supplies Unearthed from Coffin 162

The Du family from Funing Arrested Yesterday, around 6 PM, the Second Squad of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau's Water Patrol Team, based on informant reports, learned that two bandit ships were anchored near Xiaogang, Tanzigang. Police Chief Zhang Yushu and others took a patrol boat to the specified location and found two ships anchored there. They boarded the ships and conducted a search, but found no contraband. Consequently, eleven people of all ages, including Du Wuhua, Du Qingfu, Du Hua, Du Xiaokouzi, Du Xiaoguniang, Liu Jiayuan, Liu Jiaxiang, Liu Zhang, Liu Zhu, Xiao Erzi, and Xiao Sanzi, all from Funing, were taken to the branch station and then transferred to the South City Headquarters. Under strict questioning by Squad Leader Zhu, Du Chunhua confessed that he was thirty-three years old. Du Qingfu was his father and brother. Hua was his wife, and Xiaokouzi and Xiaoguniang were his children. Two days ago, a carpenter he knew named Zhou Er asked him to transport three Browning pistols, fifteen rounds of ammunition, one Mauser pistol, and forty-eight rounds of ammunition to Funing, promising to pay him fifty-three dollars after the job was done. He, in a moment of folly, agreed. However, due to the inconvenient timing, he temporarily hid the firearms in a dilapidated coffin in a remote area of Dachang, intending to transport them to Funing when the opportunity arose. When questioned, Liu Jiayuan stated that he was thirty-three years old, Zhu was his mother, Zhang was his wife, and Jiaxiang, Xiao Erzi, and Xiao Sanzi were all his sons. He was a law-abiding citizen and had never been a robber, though he sometimes stole chickens in various cities. Du Chunhua was his cousin, but he had no knowledge of Du's private transportation of military supplies. Unexpectedly, after the case was exposed, his entire family was implicated, and he pleaded for leniency. The squad was ordered to escort Du to Dachang, where he pointed out the dilapidated coffin containing the hidden firearms. After the squad returned with the weapons, they prepared a report and transferred the case to the Municipal Public Safety Bureau for further investigation.

Suspect Arrested for Robbery, Kidnapping, and Extortion 163

Zhu Heshang, also known as Zhu Liangwu, a local resident, ran the Longchang Auto Repair Shop on Chengdu Road. Recently, he was suspected of armed robbery and kidnapping for ransom. He was arrested in front of the New World Hotel the other day by Kang Zengxiang, a Chinese detective from the General Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to the police lawyer, Ru Bao Yi, the defendant was an accomplice of Dai Anxiang and Wang Jinsheng, who had already been sentenced to imprisonment by the court. At the time, the police had been searching for him without success. As the police have not yet fully investigated, they are not prosecuting him at this time but are requesting permission to detain him temporarily. Zhu hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him and requested bail. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the report and ordered the case to be adjourned for further hearing. Zhu Heshang was temporarily detained.

Han Jinsheng Commits Suicide by Drowning 164

Suffering from Economic Pressure

Death Unforeseen

Han Jinsheng, twenty-six years old, a local resident and owner of Yongxing Redwood Workshop at No. 58 Lingji Street, Dadongmen, Nanshi, has recently been affected by the war, causing sluggish business in the shop, resulting in debts of over a thousand dollars. With increasing financial difficulties and the early loss of his parents, he felt helpless and decided to end his life. Around 4 PM on the thirteenth of this month, he left the shop and disappeared without a trace. The other day, the Wusongkou Lifesaving Bureau patrol boat recovered a floating corpse from the Huangpu River. As no relatives could be found, the body was temporarily kept by the undertaker. Later, Han's older brother, Dou Dezhuan, and others learned of it and went to Songjiang to identify the body, which turned out to be Han Jinsheng. Yesterday, several of his colleagues and friends re-coffined the body and transported it to Shanghai for burial.

Publication of "Global Inspection Tour" 165

Last year, the Tianjin Dagongbao newspaper sent reporter Cao Jun Gubing to travel to Soviet Russia. Upon his return, he wrote a book titled "Inspection Tour of Soviet Russia." Because it coincided with a time when the Chinese people felt bored and wanted to study the current situation in Soviet Russia, the book quickly became popular, selling tens of thousands of copies. However, Cao Jun's account only covered one aspect of the construction of the socialist country. As for the capitalist and imperialist countries, they are currently facing economic panic, and the state of that panic is lacking a specialized book introducing it. The book "Global Inspection Tour" is the latest record of Mr. Ji Hongchang, Meng Xianzhang, Ling Mianzhi, Yu Furun, and others traveling around Asia, America, Europe, and Africa for six months from last autumn to this spring, covering about twenty countries. It describes in detail the political, military, economic, and social conditions of various countries, especially the various social problems caused by economic panic, as well as various new inventions, great engineering projects, and the current situation of millions of Chinese merchants and overseas Chinese scattered around the world. In addition to the main text of about 200,000 words, it also includes forty-six color pictures, such as the 102-story skyscraper in New York, the British naval review of hundreds of warships, and the German Zeppelin airship, which can broaden people's horizons. This book is published by the Oriental Society at No. 10 Xinping Road, Beiping. To make it accessible to the public, it is only priced at one yuan. It has been delivered to the Ri Xin Bookstore and the Shenzhou Beixin Modern Bookstore at No. 19 Baolongfang, Albert Road, for distribution. Mr. Ji and others spent about 60,000 yuan on this trip, and this book is the result. Readers only need to spend one yuan to read this book, and its effect is equivalent to spending 60,000 yuan to travel around the world.

Central Bank Inspection Report 167

No. 134

The 134th Central Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the committee is responsible for inspecting the bank's reserve for the issuance of convertible banknotes. On August 20, 1932, Supervisor Yu Qiaqing conducted the 134th inspection at the bank's issuance bureau. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible banknotes issued: 30,074,667 silver dollars, including 27,657,863 silver dollar notes and 3,082,804 auxiliary currency notes. Total amount of convertible banknote reserve: 30,074,667 silver dollars, including 25,246,667 silver dollars in cash. This cash reserve includes 22,653,152.74 silver dollars in the bank's issuance vault, 1,424,541 silver dollars in branches in various ports, and 1,168,973.26 silver dollars in other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 5,494,000 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes issued: 375,000. Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknote reserve: 375,000. This reserve includes USD 150,000, deposited in local banks, equivalent to 375,000 Customs Gold Units at a fixed rate of 40. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. August 20, 1932, Central Bank Board of Supervisors.

Achievements of the Commodity Inspection Bureau 168

The leather belts of cotton spinning mills often need to be cleaned with oxalic acid. Last year, most of the oxalic acid on the market was of inferior quality. The factories switched to buying a ready-made solution to replace it, which cost ten times more each month. Recently, the Yong'an Third Factory entrusted the Commodity Inspection Bureau to test the solution. The result was that it contained only 3% oxalic acid. Therefore, the Yong'an Third Factory purchased oxalic acid from British merchants and prepared it according to the method, saving dozens of yuan each month.

Letter to the Editor 176

To the Editor,

I am writing on behalf of Mr. Wang Xiaoshan, who claims that the news item in the Shen Bao on the 19th of this month regarding the accidental fire at the Jichangli rattan workshop in Wangjia Wharf contains many inaccuracies. According to Mr. Xiaoshan, he has been running the Yixinglong rattan workshop for more than ten years. Recently, due to busy summer business, he has been stocking more goods than usual and has fire insurance of 1,500 taels to guard against unforeseen circumstances. On the 18th, during the Ghost Festival, offerings were made on the overpass building, and when burning paper ingots, the fire somehow spread to the rattan material and caused it to ignite. He immediately directed his partners to put out the fire. The easterly wind was very strong on that day, and despite their best efforts to extinguish the flames, they were unable to do so, causing it to spread to neighboring houses, resulting in unfortunate damage. Mr. Xiaoshan is honest and sincere, as known by his neighbors, who are willing to vouch for him. The report that his business was sluggish and that he had a large amount of fire insurance in order to engage in illegal activities is untrue and may cause confusion and damage to his reputation. Therefore, he has specially entrusted our law firm to send this letter for factual correction. Accordingly, we are sending this letter, hoping that your newspaper will publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" column for correction.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Zhou Shiying
